<username>Wendel Tse< /username><time>1465182373802< /time>< Rating>
4</Rating>
< text>
I am rating this mostly for the great selection of baked goods on the one side of the market.  They make the biggest (like a ping pong paddle) & best palmiers.  They are buttery but not too crumbly, firm enough to dunk in coffee or milk like a biscotti.  And they have thick fat slices of pound cake, frisbee sized chocolate chip or peanut butter cookies.  And churros.  And much more.  They used to make great burritos to go, but stopped a few years ago, maybe because of the burrito joint next door.

Update 6/5/16:  Came here for the palmiers and shocked that they are now half the size!  Sign of the times.</text>

<Name>Gabrielle Santiago</Name>< time>
1466017975076< /time>
<Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
Imagine if a theme park churro and vanilla custard had a baby. That, my friends, is what I found here -- a beautiful vanilla custard filled churro. For just $1 a piece, you too, can find this little slice of heaven.

In all seriousness, I've been hunting down this particular churro for quite some time now. We kept getting Mexican food catered at work and they would always throw a box of these in with our large orders. I knew it wasn't from the restaurant but I never found out where they were sourcing these bad boys from. Eventually someone at work let me in on the trade secret, which is why I found myself walking into this place at lunch on a workday. Lo and behold, the churros were sitting there in all their glory behind the little acrylic doors. Not quite sure when they make them each day, but if you're lucky enough to get them fresh..well, let's just say you've hit the jackpot.

I didn't get to explore any other part of the store or try any other pastries solely because I came here for one thing and one thing only (lol), but if I were basing it on that alone then this place gets the nod of approval from me. Only downside is that it does have a credit card minimum of $5 but who am I kidding? That just means you can get 5 churros for yourself and not feel bad about it hehe.< /Review>

1527441298909</Time>
< Rate>
3</Rate>
<Review>Thursday night in Downtown Placentia 8:22pm.  Place is a ghost town.  Maybe it's because we're close to closing time at 9pm. Owner/cook is just chillin watching Swamp people on the TV.  Ok. He greets us and says we can sit anywhere we like.

We're greeted by the waitress, our order was taken and we were given some excellent salsa and chips. My wife and I order carne asada fries, 2 birria tacos, 2 tacos de pollo and one quesadilla.

The portions on carne asada fries were huge! But the fries were dry and somewhat rubbery. Don't know if the  fries were cooked long enough. Good flavor though. Quesadilla was a significant size, but lacked flavor. Yes, a quesadilla is just tortilla and cheese but it makes a difference on what type of cheese is used.  The tacos, (birria) had good flavor profile and looked carefully manicured. Portions were a bit on the small side for the price. ($1.65 for the basic tortilla and $2.25 for hand made tortilla). I guess I'm just used to the normal overstuffed tacos with the meat, cilantro and onions hanging over the side of the tortilla.

All in all it's fair. Maybe we need to come at a different time instead of 30-40 min before closing time. Wouldn't go out of my way to make it here, but if I'm in the area I might give it a try again.<//Review>< pictures>

< text>
There are several Mexican restaurants in Old Town Placentia, including one that seemingly everyone says is the best not just here, but for miles. This however, is our favorite, though admittedly we've many left to try.
Not among the fanciest but it is bright and clean and for flavor, generous portions, and price, not to mention fast friendly service, it's going to take quite a bit to find a better place.
It is my habit, on an initial visit to have my goto combo. Shredded beef enchiladas, rice and beans. The beef was well seasoned and the colorado (it"s a color, not a state üòä) was a deep red and among the best I've had elsewhere. The sided were ample with a generous amount of cheese on the beans. In translation the food lives up to the tasty name. SABROSO, INDEED!< /text>

<review>Great space, chill vibe, tasty bowl, reasonable price,  quick service, inspiring quotes on the wall, rad merch displays, cute menu design... they had it all... But I still would not give them 5 stars because my overall experience was NOT exceptional and I think it wouldn't have taken much to get there.

The reasons are probably too subtle or personal for a Google review, and not pointed towards this cafe in particular, but California (&America) in general.

So here we go, here is my FREE guide to all WHITE business owners on being a little more racially inclusive in your thoughts/words/actions. (Please share the kindness with your peers, Sambazon)

1. Be friendly with tourists. Someone coming to your store for the very first time from a different continent is simultaneously experiencing a new culture, new food and new people, so be gentle and patient with their questions.

2. If you cannot recognise an outsider, here's a simple clue, look at their skin colour or listen to their accent. Tip:  It's a great way to start a fun  conversation by trying to guess where they may be from :)

3. Take a little extra effort to smile and make them feel welcome. You may not even be conscious of it but we experience it every day as coloured customers in white establishments. Staff at the counter smile at everyone in the line but when it comes to our turn, it's like they suddenly forget to smile

4. Listen harder and try again if you didn't catch their name the first time because of their strange accent, or the white/christian filters in your brain. Ask them how to spell it and how to pronounce it. They will love you to the moon and back.

5. When their order is ready, call out their funny sounding and awkward name loudly and clearly. If you forgot how to pronounce it or you weren't the one taking the order, take a few steps, walk up to their table and apologize for being stuck in your white bubble and not being comfortable to pronounce their üëΩ name. This could be a bloody game changer for you, your customers, your staff and society in general. Next time, please try it.

6. (Optional Bonus Tip) If you didn't do any of the above right, walk up to their table when you have a free moment and ask if they are having a good time. Not in a superficial customer service way but a sincere and caring way. Of course, you could only do this if you had a little extra time between taking and making orders all day, so if you can't do this, it's totally fine.

7. If you are kind and friendly with single female customers but don't give a (insert preferred expletive) about single male customers, that's kinda sexist, so change that.

Good luck with your business! Let's make the world a more friendly place for everyone! ‚òÆÔ∏è</review>< Pics>

<time>1422483934920<//time><Rate>4</Rate>< review>
I LOVE this place, but I'm still only going to give it 4-stars, (you'll see why as you read on further).

PARKING: Depending on when you go, there may be parking close by. The parking lot is pretty small, but I guess it's just enough to accommodate all of the business in that same plaza area.

ACAI BOWLS: The reason why my husband and I stop by when we're in the general vicinity. Their Acai Bowls are so good here. You have to try one here! They come in different combinations. Prices are steep, but they don't skimp on the portion sizes or the quality of the ingredients. Even just getting a Medium-sized bowl is a LOT. I like the Rio Bowl. :)

ATMOSPHERE: Fairly chic, almost has a coffee-house vibe to it. If there were outlets, it would be the perfect spot for me to work with my laptop during the day. But....

LAYOUT: The place is pretty small. Not too many indoor tables to go around. There are tables outside, but they've all been in use the 5 times I've been here. Which is too bad for me... :( I would've loved to just sit and chill, and order something else from there menu if I was there for more than a couple of hours after finishing my bowl.

LOCATION: The beach is close by! I've never tried it yet, but I'm wondering if it's accessible by walking since it looks like it's the next block over.....< /review>

<review>Sambazon's first venture into a storefront Caf√©. I actually expected quite a bit from a company I like so much. First off they make great products that are healthy and were generous to a fundraising event at my rock climbing gym in Orange County.

I wanted to go to the Grand Opening, but was too busy, turns out it's been open for a bit and there was the Grand Celebration event. One of the employee's said their dad came in a lot at first to check in on them, but seems to have fallen in love with it and goes whether they are working or not.

It's not a smoothi bar, it's not Jamba Juice, it truly is an Acai Caf√© with tons of room for an expanded menu and such a unique flavor that it should shortly become the Acai capital of San Diego.

For such a large company to not seek the wisdom of a Franchise consultant on how to design, properly train and manage a new store of employees is beyond me. Honestly I could memorize all the ingredients and menu in a matter of minutes and retool the efficiency of the store in a few hours. Business practices that work at a storefront to not translate from sales and marketing.

I went here for a little lunch dessert and decided against the pure dessert bowl and went with Machado's PB & Banana Bowl. The reasoning behind that is if you've ever made your own smoothie from their packs versus the bottles the bottles have apple juice which imo is too fruity and counters the purity of the acai. Plus it's the largest calorie producer in their drinks. This was the bowl and it was dessert, but I wanted chocolate still. Smooth peanut butter, had to have been organic everything else was and it's kinda in their culture here. Crunchy granola, peanut butter, chocolate hemp milk was interesting if you've never had it. It's got much more of a pure chocolate taste than chocolate flavored milk does.

I could have gone crazy making tons of concoctions and like many Coastal shops encourages the customization. If I lived closer and could frequent it more I'd definitely promote my favorite concoction and try to get it on the menu along with the other famous celebs.< /review>< pics>

<Review>On the one hand, I want to give this place 5 stars.  On the other, I don't want anyone else to find this gem and keep it all to myself.  Converted officer in office park, the front room is mostly Golden/bronze/silver age goodies, with stacks of 50 centers in several rooms in back- there's a marvel room, dc, room, etc.  The back rooms are semi organized by character/title but for the most part you are hunting.  I found serval comics in the back that I literally have not been able to find anywhere on the internet at any price, let alone 50 cents.  I think it was 70 bucks to fill a box with whatever you want, saw several people doing that.  Friendly staff and the owner is super reasonable on pricing. < name>
Marco Diaz< /name>
<date>1621454497905< /date><rating>2< /rating>< Review>
This place is not the best party supply store for their lack of organization, high prices, and check out practices.

To start off, they got me with the free parking. I should have known that nothing is free. I saw the sign and thought it would be great. As soon as I walked in I saw how disorganized the place was. The line was already taking up an aisle of the store and boxes where open everywhere. The next issue where the prices, when I know for a fact that other stores had similar pinatas for $15 this place had them starting at 20 and 25 for the two I grabbed. With guilt for already parking there I decided to eat the cost. Several candy and items where similarly very high priced, so this is not the place to come get a bargain. Bedies, the employees grabbing pinatas where kind and helpful even through they didn't have a single clue where any character pinata was. There was zero organization and they were constantly being followed by 4 to 5 customers asking where specific pinatas where.

The biggest issue was a result of the cashier. For such a big warehouse with customers packed like rats along the aisles you would think they would have more than one cashier or their fastest person. The opposite, they had a guy who was comically slow if it wasn't for the 40 minute line wait I had to endure. This was like a SNL sketch, he would scan items and when he didn't know he would ask the owner "Kennia" and then repeat the price to the customer who obviously heard her. They really need to get someone that can check the customers out quickly and efficiently so the store can clear out. Last but most importantly they imposed a made up fee on my cc for using a certain card. They said they were being charged that by the credit card, and they were passing the charge onto me. As a merchant that is the cost of doing business, you don't punish me for paying with legal tender in credit card form.

If you are looking for party supplies at a reasonable price, avoid this tourist trap. The free parking comes out more expensive with their unreasonably high prices and credit card fees.</Review>

< Review>
Cozy little dinner. Breakfast is a specialty and available all day. The food was served quickly. The chicken fried steak is so huge and delicious too. They have a varied selection of 3 egg omelets to choose from or they will create one to include your favorite items. Fresh baked biscuits pair well with gravy. The biscuits are smaller than others, but they offer them in servings of two, four or more. Our waiter was delightful and attended all our needs. I like the automated system they use. The waiter enters your order on a tablet and if you pay with a credit card, it never leaves your sight since the waiter can swipe your card with his tablet at your table.< /Review>
